  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c202fb2a-db79-4a47-a64a-e81a34d3d8c4'

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer9055454954144246787">Twelve-year-old Aru Shah has a tendency to stretch the truth in order to fit in at school. While her classmates are jetting off to family vacations in exotic locales, she'll be spending her autumn break at home, in the Museum of Ancient Indian Art and Culture, waiting for her mom to return from her latest archeological trip. Is it any wonder that Aru makes up stories about</span>
  <span id="freeText9055454954144246787" style="display:none">Twelve-year-old Aru Shah has a tendency to stretch the truth in order to fit in at school. While her classmates are jetting off to family vacations in exotic locales, she'll be spending her autumn break at home, in the Museum of Ancient Indian Art and Culture, waiting for her mom to return from her latest archeological trip. Is it any wonder that Aru makes up stories about being royalty, traveling to Paris, and having a chauffeur?<br /><br />One day, three schoolmates show up at Aru's doorstep to catch her in a lie. They don't believe her claim that the museum's Lamp of Bharata is cursed, and they dare Aru to prove it. <i>Just a quick light,</i> Aru thinks. Then she can get herself out of this mess and <i>never ever</i> fib again.<br /><br />But lighting the lamp has dire consequences. She unwittingly frees the Sleeper, an ancient demon whose duty it is to awaken the God of Destruction. Her classmates and beloved mother are frozen in time, and it's up to Aru to save them.<br /><br />The only way to stop the demon is to find the reincarnations of the five legendary Pandava brothers, protagonists of the Hindu epic poem, the <i>Mahabharata</i>, and journey through the Kingdom of Death. But how is one girl in Spider-Man pajamas supposed to do all <i>that</i>?</span>
  <a data-text-id="9055454954144246787" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">There's Hanuman and Urvashi, and Indra and Yama make a brief appearance as well! The book is about Aru Shah and her quest to save the world, so althou<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">There's Hanuman and Urvashi, and Indra and Yama make a brief appearance as well! The book is about Aru Shah and her quest to save the world, so although it weaves together a lot of Indian mythology (especially regarding the Pandavas), the novel itself is entirely from Chokshi's imagination.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">No, these are separate from the Riordan verse as said by Rick himself.<br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://rickriordan.com/2018/01/rick-riordan-presents-gets-underway/'>http://rickriordan.com/2018/01/rick-r...</a><br/>"These are original stories generated by<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">No, these are separate from the Riordan verse as said by Rick himself.<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://rickriordan.com/2018/01/rick-riordan-presents-gets-underway/">http://rickriordan.com/2018/01/rick-r...</a><br />"These are original stories generated by the authors – their intellectual property, told their way, with their characters and their sense of humor. The worlds they create are their own. They are not extensions of Percy Jackson’s world."<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_2544982929" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2544982929" />
    <a title="chai ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42130592-chai"><img alt="chai ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603167303p2/42130592.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2544982929?book_show_action=true">Nov 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="chai ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="chai ♡" href="/user/show/42130592-chai">chai ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=2018-releases">2018-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=own-voices">own-voices</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=poc-rep">poc-rep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2544982929" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16351684933748654020">I finished this book feeling the extreme weight of doing something remarkable for my older self to be nostalgic about, and, also realizing that the one thing all different mythologies seem to have in common is that apparently all gods just live for drama.<br/><br/><strong>
  <u>So, what’s this book about?</u>
</strong><br/><br/><em>Aru Shah and The End of Time</em> begins with a bad idea, and bad ideas begin, as most bad ideas do, with a <em>dare</em>.<br/><br/>Aru Shah likes to bend the truth. That was what her classmates meant when they called her <em>a liar</em>, and they</span>
  <span id="freeText16351684933748654020" style="display:none">I finished this book feeling the extreme weight of doing something remarkable for my older self to be nostalgic about, and, also realizing that the one thing all different mythologies seem to have in common is that apparently all gods just live for drama.<br /><br /><strong>
  <u>So, what’s this book about?</u>
</strong><br /><br /><em>Aru Shah and The End of Time</em> begins with a bad idea, and bad ideas begin, as most bad ideas do, with a <em>dare</em>.<br /><br />Aru Shah likes to bend the truth. That was what her classmates meant when they called her <em>a liar</em>, and they weren’t wrong, but they missed the main point. Aru was a “liar” in more profound a way than they knew. Aru lives with her curator mother in the Museum of Ancient Indian Art and Culture in Atlanta, and she had for so long fed her mind on stories that if you could wander into it, you would discover a fantasia. Aru just didn’t expect her real life to intersect with fiction. She might have intentionally lit the supposedly cursed Lamp of Bharata and unintentionally released the demonic Sleeper from his slumber, prompting the end of the world. She might really be the reincarnation of one of the Pandava brothers, famous demigods, and she might even force her mind to expand outward and believe that Mini, a complete stranger, is her newly found “soul sister”, her guardian angel is a grumpy pigeon named Subala (“Boo” to aggravate him) and the fate of the universe lies in the hands of two clueless twelve-year-old.<br /><br />But surely, there must be some fundamental rule of the universe that forbids you set off on quests in your <em>Spider-Man pajamas</em> because that’s where Aru draws the line.<br /><blockquote>
  <em>“Sometimes you don't even know how special you might be. Sometimes it takes moments of horror or happiness to, if you will, unleash that knowledge.” </em>
</blockquote><br />It's startling to take stock of how of a piece this book feels with the Percy Jackson series, of what a complicated dance of intermeshing nostalgias this book stirs and explores.<br /><br /><em>Aru Shah and The End of Time</em> is a tapestry woven together by threads from Hindu cosmology and folklore, and Chokshi has successfully plumbed a lesser-represented mythology and written an immersive world that is described in such exquisite manner and given such a measure of life that it seizes the imagination like a drug. The whole is an uplifting, joyful story that is chock-full of witty banter and pop-culture references that left me in an uncommonly good mood.<br /><br />Aru fell tumbling inside a story and simultaneously writing it all around her, and not alone but with someone—Mini—who just happened to be as brave and magical as a fairy tale made real. I absolutely loved their friendship. Two sides of the same coin, they stumbled upon each other, in a collision, as though they had long been wandering in the same labyrinth and had finally rounded the corner that would bring them face-to-face. Saving the world, as we all know, is traditionally a dull affair made cheery only by having someone else to keep you company. And in spite of the chill that didn’t quite leave them as the ill-omened day creeps closer, I love how they were still well able to marvel at their latest unfolding of their life.<br /><br /><em>Aru Shah and The End of Time</em> is delightful and assertive and proud and makes me want to read more of this story for more of these voices, connections and lives. Fans of Percy Jackson will absolutely love it, and new readers will be mesmerized by this imaginative and enticing world!<br /><blockquote>
  <em>“A particularly good book has a way of opening new spaces in one's mind. It even invited you to come back later and rummage through what you'd learn.”</em>
</blockquote><br />Finally, can we just take a moment to appreciate the fact that Rick Riordan has apparently gotten tons of letters asking him to, "please write about Indian mythology! do the Maya mythology next!" and he was like, "those aren't my stories to tell but let me find you own voices writers who CAN write these books for you so you get to see your culture represented and valued too!" and now this good dude is heading up his own imprint of more mythology books for kids and using his white privilege to enhance and empower the voices of authors from marginalized communities?<br /><br />I respect one (1) man.<br /><br /><blockquote>✨ <a href="http://amzn.eu/9Jnbkf3" rel="nofollow noopener">wishlist</a> ✨ <a href="https://runawaywithdreamthieves.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a> ✨ <a href="https://twitter.com/kzabrekker" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a> ✨ <a href="https://azqaban.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">tumblr</a> ✨</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="16351684933748654020" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2285474537" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2285474537" />
    <a title="Rick Riordan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25375513-rick-riordan"><img alt="Rick Riordan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442449448p2/25375513.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2285474537?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rick Riordan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rick Riordan" href="/user/show/25375513-rick-riordan">Rick Riordan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2285474537" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12579504338941201845">Have you ever read a book and thought, "Wow, I wish I'd written that!"? <br/><br/>For me, Aru Shah and the End of Time is one of those books. It has everything I like: humor, action, great characters and, of course, awesome mythology! But this is not a book I could have written. I just don't have the expertise or the insider's knowledge to tackle the huge incredible world of Hindu mythology, much less make it so fun and reader-friendly.<br/><br/>Fortunately for all of us, Roshani Chokshi does.<br/><br/>If you are not familia</span>
  <span id="freeText12579504338941201845" style="display:none">Have you ever read a book and thought, "Wow, I wish I'd written that!"? <br /><br />For me, Aru Shah and the End of Time is one of those books. It has everything I like: humor, action, great characters and, of course, awesome mythology! But this is not a book I could have written. I just don't have the expertise or the insider's knowledge to tackle the huge incredible world of Hindu mythology, much less make it so fun and reader-friendly.<br /><br />Fortunately for all of us, Roshani Chokshi does.<br /><br />If you are not familiar with Hindu mythology - wow, are you in for a treat! You thought Zeus, Ares and Apollo were wild? Wait until you meet Hanuman and Urvashi. You thought Riptide was a cool weapon? Check out this fine assortment of divine astras - maces, swords, bows, and nets woven from lightning. Take your pick. You're going to need them. You thought Medusa was scary? She's got nothing on the nagini and rakshas. Aru Shah, a salty and smart seventh grade girl from New Jersey, is about to plunge into the midst of all this craziness, and her adventure will make your head explode in the best possible way.<br /><br />If you already know Hindu mythology, you're about to have the most entertaining family reunion ever. You're going to see lots of your favorites - gods, demons, monsters, villains, heroes. You're going to soar up to the heavens and down into the Underworld. And no matter how many of these myths you already know, I'll bet you a pack of Twizzlers you're going to learn something new. <br /><br />Can you tell I'm excited to share this book with you? Yeah, I'm pretty excited. <br /><br />So what are you waiting for? GET THIS BOOK!<br /><br />When we first meet Aru Shah, she is hanging out in the Indian-American Museum where her mom works. School vacation has started, and Aru is pretty sure it's going to be a boring day. Yikes. She is SO wrong.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12579504338941201845" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2372127680" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2372127680" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2372127680?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=diversity-yay">diversity-yay</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=sidekicks">sidekicks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=quest">quest</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2372127680" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11396434741049886809">This book is trying too hard.<br/><br/>I never managed to <i>truly</i> and <i>effectively</i> get a full sense of Aru Shah’s personality, because the voice of the author is far more present and loud. <br/><br/>And still, somehow, I managed to dislike Aru. She made me cringe so many times that at some point I was questioning if I was this annoying at the age of twelve. I don’t think I thought about picking my nose every day like Aru does. <br/><br/>It is somewhat interesting from start to finish, that I will admit. The mythology spiked my </span>
  <span id="freeText11396434741049886809" style="display:none">This book is trying too hard.<br /><br />I never managed to <i>truly</i> and <i>effectively</i> get a full sense of Aru Shah’s personality, because the voice of the author is far more present and loud. <br /><br />And still, somehow, I managed to dislike Aru. She made me cringe so many times that at some point I was questioning if I was this annoying at the age of twelve. I don’t think I thought about picking my nose every day like Aru does. <br /><br />It is somewhat interesting from start to finish, that I will admit. The mythology spiked my interest and I was curious to see how Aru and her new friend would go about saving the world from the mess Aru created by awakening a demon. <br /><br />But it’s also extremely disappointing, seeing that the only character I adored was Boo and, well, he’s a pigeon. Yes, I have a crush on a pigeon, how weird and pathetic is that? I mean, he is incredibly cute and the only fully-fleshed character, as ironic as that sounds. <br /><br />We also meet other characters along the way, but the problem is they never stay for long, and definitely not long enough for us to form a deep connection to them, plus the majority of mythological creatures in here are either mean or think too highly of themselves. I get it, you’re… important, but you don’t have to remind us every five seconds. <br /><br />I am actually shocked I didn’t enjoy this, having absolutely loved the author’s <i>The Star-Touched Queen</i> duology. Perhaps those of you who couldn’t stand the purple prose in that one will find this story more pleasant, since the only thing that’s purple about this book is 1/5 of its cover. <br /><br />For those of you who wonder if it’s as good as any of Rick Riordan’s works, it’s not. It tries to be <i>Percy Jackson</i> here and there, but it fails miserably, and besides, I don’t believe it should have tried to begin with.<br /><br />If only Aru Shah had been a relatable kid and her friend Mini less mousy and a sidekick, I would have ended up loving this to pieces most likely.<br /><br />But hey, at least there’s the pigeon to look forward to meeting. Oh, I am so, so sad. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11396434741049886809" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2178737254" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2178737254" />
    <a title="kav (xreadingsolacex)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54570527-kav-xreadingsolacex"><img alt="kav (xreadingsolacex)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585981757p2/54570527.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2178737254?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="kav (xreadingsolacex)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="kav (xreadingsolacex)" href="/user/show/54570527-kav-xreadingsolacex">kav (xreadingsolacex)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54570527-kav-xreadingsolacex?shelf=dif-religions-rep">dif-religions-rep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54570527-kav-xreadingsolacex?shelf=disaster-mcs">disaster-mcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54570527-kav-xreadingsolacex?shelf=south-asian-fiction">south-asian-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54570527-kav-xreadingsolacex?shelf=bad-bitches">bad-bitches</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54570527-kav-xreadingsolacex?shelf=stories-of-hope">stories-of-hope</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54570527-kav-xreadingsolacex?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54570527-kav-xreadingsolacex?shelf=asian-fiction">asian-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54570527-kav-xreadingsolacex?shelf=found-family">found-family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54570527-kav-xreadingsolacex?shelf=indian-american-fiction">indian-american-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2178737254" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12311736684714883452"><b>Disclaimer: I received an ARC from the publisher in exchange for an honest review. This is no way impacts my review.</b><br/><br/><i>Aru Shah and the End of the Time</i> is a middle-grade fantasy novel based off of Hindu mythology, following a 12-year old girl, Aru Shah, who finds out she is a reincarnation of one of the five Pandava brothers and essentially has to change the world.<br/><br/>If 12-year old me had had the ability to read a book like this, maybe I wouldn't have been ashamed of my heritage growing up because soc</span>
  <span id="freeText12311736684714883452" style="display:none"><b>Disclaimer: I received an ARC from the publisher in exchange for an honest review. This is no way impacts my review.</b><br /><br /><i>Aru Shah and the End of the Time</i> is a middle-grade fantasy novel based off of Hindu mythology, following a 12-year old girl, Aru Shah, who finds out she is a reincarnation of one of the five Pandava brothers and essentially has to change the world.<br /><br />If 12-year old me had had the ability to read a book like this, maybe I wouldn't have been ashamed of my heritage growing up because society told me that being Indian wasn't good enough. So to all the 12-year old Indian and/or Hindu kids who are going to read this book, you deserve to feel the way I never got to feel-proud of your heritage.<br /><br /><i>Aru Shah and the End of Time</i> is not only one of the most important books I've ever read, it's also one of the best. From the plot to the characters to the writing, it is downright incredible in every way. <br /><br />Let's start by talking about the characters. Our main character, Aru Shah, is a girl who lies <b>a lot</b>. And I loved that. I loved the creation of her character because it was unlike any middle-grade protagonist I have ever seen before.<br /><br />Aru is not your classic heroine. She essentially causes the mess that sets off this books. She isn't a morally grey heroine because she is without a doubt good, but she is a pre-teen who doesn't necessarily understand good and bad and who just wants to be excited by the popular kids, but isn't. And then her world changes forever.<br /><br />Then there's our other primary character, Mini. Mini is part-Filipina and part-Indian, knows way too much about medical stuff, and is Aru's "soul-sister." <br /><br />I loved Mini just as much as I loved Aru. She, unlike Aru, is much more a classic heroine who you would root for, but she still has intricate details woven into her-such as her obsession with how anything and everything can make you sick and how smart she is. <br /><br />And as these two characters are working together and are essentially sisters we get a huge dose of girls supporting girls in this book which I live for. If there's a trope we need to see more of, it's that one.<br /><br />And of course, we have some other great characters in this novel. Boo, the girls pigeon guardian. Hanuman and Urvashi, part of the Council, the girls godly parents (which I'm not spoiling for you, you have to read and find out which reincarnations they are), and more. Each supporting character, villian, etc. had their own tone that made them their own character, no matter how big or small their part was.<br /><br />And now, for the plot.<br /><br />Listen, if you gave me this and Percy Jackson to choose from, no offense but I would choose this novel (not that I don't love Percy he's also rad).<br /><br />Like I said, this is the book 12-year old me needed but never got.<br /><br />The journey the characters go on in this novel was such a fun one to be a part of, but let me just say I got freaked out time and again hoping our heroines would survive the countless demons they faced. <br /><br />Something that I think was really crucial to how much I enjoyed the plot was the pacing. The pacing in this novel is <b>exquisite</b>. That's all I can really say without spoilers, but I just really loved the pacing.<br /><br />And also, how it tied in Hindu mythology to the plot. There were parts when I honestly thought I might cry because of how much it related to me growing up. And all the different stops Aru and Mini made on their way to defeat the over-arching antagonist of this novel were so fun to read.<br /><br />I have been anticipating this novel with every bone in my body. I have been aching for it to be in my possession. I literally almost cried when it was announced. And it did not disappoint. It exceeded my expectations.<br /><br />So please, read this novel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12311736684714883452" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4434568257476993034"><b>This was absolutely EVERYTHING I hoped it would be!</b> Just afjdklsd forget how old I am for a second: I love love love the Percy Jackson books. (Except for <i>you</i>, Mr. Burning Maze. Go fix all your typos because That Character definitely did not die. I am in denial.) I go to Riordan stories for (a) humour, (b) loveable adorkable characters, and (c) epic mythology but with an absurdist and cleverly witty twist. And what did Aru Shah do?!<br/><br/>ALL OF THAT. Perfectly.<br/><br/>Since this is a Riordan imprint, I just wa</span>
  <span id="freeText4434568257476993034" style="display:none"><b>This was absolutely EVERYTHING I hoped it would be!</b> Just afjdklsd forget how old I am for a second: I love love love the Percy Jackson books. (Except for <i>you</i>, Mr. Burning Maze. Go fix all your typos because That Character definitely did not die. I am in denial.) I go to Riordan stories for (a) humour, (b) loveable adorkable characters, and (c) epic mythology but with an absurdist and cleverly witty twist. And what did Aru Shah do?!<br /><br />ALL OF THAT. Perfectly.<br /><br />Since this is a Riordan imprint, I just wanted to open with that sentiment, because it really has the Percy Jackson feel and voice (!!) and I'm just super excited Riordan is sharing this and bringing minority #ownvoices authors under his banner to share their stories in correct and beautifully told ways.<br /><br />ok ok afjkdsd so you get it: I quite enjoyed this. I won't ramble for ages (WOW A SHOCKING PROMISE) but here are the main things I loved...<br /><br />➸ <b>Aru was just a freaking amazing little squish.</b> She has a big imagination (read: she lies a lot lol lol) and she did the entire quest in Spiderman pyjamas. She's awkward and cute and struggling with doubts and wants as well as being totally confident at times and yelling at demons and making deals with ancient gods.<br />➸ <b>Also MINI...she's the other reincarnated Pandava.</b> She's like a germaphobe and is always saying "if you do that, we'll all die!!" and she's adorable and I loved her. I also loved their friendship growing to such a tight-knit sister bond.<br />➸ <b>THE GODS AND MYTHOLOGY!!</b> I very much don't know much Indian mythology so I learned a lot plus I love the way it was presented. Also Aru was equal parts reverent of the myths and also sassed about them too and I think that's adorable.<br />➸ <b>Quest plot!! Adventure!! Journey!! Near death experiences!!</b> As does happen. It was all really fun and the pacing was great...although I do think it was kinda long. But I'm impatient lmao.<br />➸ <b>It's hinting we'll meet more Pandava sisters soon and I am excited.</b> I also loved Boo, the snarky side-kick guide pigeon, and all the messages about belonging, feeling ignored and invisible, wanting friends, and loving your found-family.<br /><br />Yes thank you, I will take more of this. :')</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15323179298893453231"><b>Actual Rating: 4.25 stars</b><br/><br/>*** Full review now posted ***<br/><br/> <i>“Tales are slippery, her mother had often said. The truth of a story depends on who is telling it.” </i><br/><br/>Aru Shah and the End of Time is the kind of book that I would have killed for when I was younger. I mean it has the fast pacing just perfect for a middle grade book, a very good writing style, Indian mythology (How cool!) and a beautiful cover!!<br/><br/>Not only that, this book was hilarious, I was laughing out loud more than one time and if you know </span>
  <span id="freeText15323179298893453231" style="display:none"><b>Actual Rating: 4.25 stars</b><br><br>*** Full review now posted ***<br><br> <i>“Tales are slippery, her mother had often said. The truth of a story depends on who is telling it.” </i><br><br>Aru Shah and the End of Time is the kind of book that I would have killed for when I was younger. I mean it has the fast pacing just perfect for a middle grade book, a very good writing style, Indian mythology (How cool!) and a beautiful cover!!<br><br>Not only that, this book was hilarious, I was laughing out loud more than one time and if you know me enough, you'd have known by this time that Satan took my soul long ago and I am an emotionless creature now! The good things don't stop here, this was devoid of all the love drama which is so good for a change! And did I mention that it had many modern references for other books and TV shows!<br><br>And if you are into mythologies, then this will surely satisfy your needs...<br>No wonder Rick Riordan presented this as it was so good and reminded me of Percy Jackson but in a different way!<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1523201773i/25344777._SX540_.jpg" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I can't wait for book 2 to be released as I am most definitely continuing this series!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15323179298893453231" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3610025258" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3610025258" />
    <a title="megs_bookrack" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack"><img alt="megs_bookrack" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532027727p2/48328025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3610025258?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="megs_bookrack" class="user" itemprop="url" name="megs_bookrack" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack">megs_bookrack</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48328025-megs-bookrack?shelf=believathon-iii">believathon-iii</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3610025258" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1573977470040086681"><b>**3.5-stars rounded up**</b><br/><br/>12-year old, Aru Shah, doesn't quite fit in. It's not just the odd fact that she and her Mom live in an actual Museum, <i>The Museum of Ancient Indian Art and Culture</i>, there are other factors as well.<br/><br/>For one, Aru attends a school where the vast majority of children are very, very wealthy. It's clear to them all that Aru is not, although she has pretended to be from time to time. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1605212401ra/30369863.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Aru sometimes feels ignored and neglected at home as well. Her Mom frequently travels procuring a</span>
  <span id="freeText1573977470040086681" style="display:none"><b>**3.5-stars rounded up**</b><br><br>12-year old, Aru Shah, doesn't quite fit in. It's not just the odd fact that she and her Mom live in an actual Museum, <i>The Museum of Ancient Indian Art and Culture</i>, there are other factors as well.<br><br>For one, Aru attends a school where the vast majority of children are very, very wealthy. It's clear to them all that Aru is not, although she has pretended to be from time to time. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1605212401ra/30369863.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Aru sometimes feels ignored and neglected at home as well. Her Mom frequently travels procuring artifacts for the museum, but even when she is around, Aru doesn't garner much attention from her.<br><br>This aspect of the story was fairly frustrating to read about actually. I wanted to grab her Mom and shake her, but I digress.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449109167ra/17235922.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Aru feels lonely and frequently embellishes stories about her life, in order to gain attention or acceptance from her peers.<br><br>Unfortunately, she does it so much, she has a bit of a reputation as a liar.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1505029162ra/23868362.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When three classmates show up at the museum and challenge Aru to prove the validity of one of the stories she has told, that the <i>Lamp of Bharata</i> is cursed, she feels compelled to light it.<br><br>A lamp she has been told, numerous times, in no uncertain terms, to never, ever light. Yeah, she lights that.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1502298014ra/23547859.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Even though it is only for a moment, this one act ends up putting the entire fate of the world in jeopardy by freeing the demon trapped inside.<br><br>The demon, known as the Sleeper, is tasked with awakening the God of Destruction, who, as the name implies, will destroy everything. Luckily, the rest of the world is frozen in time, providing Aru with a chance to undo what she's done.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1605212250ra/30369857.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Aru sets out on an epic quest, along with some new friends, to try to stop the Sleeper. <br><br>Tying in the legends of the Hindu epic poem, <i>The Mahabharata</i>, <i>Aru Shah and the End of the Time</i> is a fast-paced adventure, full of heart and valuable lessons.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1605212250ra/30369858.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I had a lot of fun with this story and can definitely see why it is so popular.<br><br>Parts of it were a bit too chaotic for my tastes, but overall, I felt it was really well done.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1501924470ra/23510571.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Aru, as a character, was interesting. I had so much sympathy for her. I felt bad for her. It hurt my heart how alone she felt in the world.<br><br>I am hoping in the next book, her Mother redeems herself a little bit, because after this one, I'm pretty much furious at her. Sure, I understand she had her reasons for what she did, but they're not good enough for me.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1605212250ra/30369859.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I did love the relationship between Aru and Mini. It was so pure. Pretty much every moment with Mini filled my heart with glee. She's just so precious.<br><br>I definitely plan to continue on with this series. I am hoping to learn so much more about these characters, this world and the myths and legends behind it.<br><br>Honestly, I feel the whole <i>Rick Riordan Imprint</i> is a gift.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1605212250ra/30369860.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="1573977470040086681" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

One day after making a bet Aru accidentally unleashes a demon god that has the capability to destroy the world. This book is how she stops him.<br/><br/>Along the way we meet Subala the pigeon (my personal favourite character) and Mini who is also gifted like Aru - the girls are Pandavas: reincarnations of famous Indian heroes with ancestors related to the gods.<br/><br/>This no</span>
  <span id="freeText15225053374573167746" style="display:none">Okay for a middle grade/children’s book I absolutely fell in love with this. <br /><br />Aru is a very imaginative girl who lives in an Indian museum. One day after making a bet Aru accidentally unleashes a demon god that has the capability to destroy the world. This book is how she stops him.<br /><br />Along the way we meet Subala the pigeon (my personal favourite character) and Mini who is also gifted like Aru - the girls are Pandavas: reincarnations of famous Indian heroes with ancestors related to the gods.<br /><br />This novel was so interesting and learning about Indian culture and mythology was so interesting!         <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2337038239" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16601200058361034095">This is my latest favorite of this year!<br/><br/>It's so difficult to get a book with Indian characters, let alone a fantasy one. Along with Hindu mythology, it's unheard of. Thank the Gods and Goddesses, for Roshani Chokshi, is here. <br/><br/>I absolutely loved this book! I adored the characters, Aru and Mini. I love Mini even more than Aru. She is allergic to almost everything and has a freaking Epi-pen! It's so good to finally see a character who is truly a human today, not like the always-perfect characters i</span>
  <span id="freeText16601200058361034095" style="display:none">This is my latest favorite of this year!<br /><br />It's so difficult to get a book with Indian characters, let alone a fantasy one. Along with Hindu mythology, it's unheard of. Thank the Gods and Goddesses, for Roshani Chokshi, is here. <br /><br />I absolutely loved this book! I adored the characters, Aru and Mini. I love Mini even more than Aru. She is allergic to almost everything and has a freaking Epi-pen! It's so good to finally see a character who is truly a human today, not like the always-perfect characters in YA novels. Talk about diversity! This book is full of that!<br /><br />I love how Chokshi incorporates the Hindu mythology. As I am a Hindu, I know a LOT of this mythology. I always love the myth of Pandavas and Kauravas. I want more of the Hindu Gods and Goddesses. If you think Zeus is powerful, you haven't heard about the Trinity Lords Shiva, Vishnu, and Brahma. <br /><br />I can now see why Rick Riordan published this book! It's so like his books with the same sense of humor, down to the titles. <br /><br />Ah! How great it is to hear the full Indian names like Arundati and Yamini, not the americanized Indian names. <br /><br />Now I am thrilled to read the sequel!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16601200058361034095" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2288061790" />
    <a title="ambsreads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30813900-ambsreads"><img alt="ambsreads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508924675p2/30813900.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2288061790?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ambsreads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ambsreads" href="/user/show/30813900-ambsreads">ambsreads</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2288061790" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10350028117196371982"><a href='https://www.ambsreads.wordpress.com/2018/04/22/aru-shah-and-the-end-of-time-by-roshani-chokshi-review/' rel='nofollow noopener'>FIND MY REVIEW FOR ARU SHAH AND THE END OF TIME ON MY BLOG. CLICK HERE TO SEE MORE</a><br/><br/>I think I’ve made it pretty clear over time that I am a big fan of Rick Riordan. I love mythology and I love learning through his books. When Riordan announced that he was going to publish own voices authors take on mythology I was beyond excited. Aru Shah and the End of Time was no exception of this. I fell in love, fast. One reason was that it was a female lead, something we don’t typically see in Riordan’s work.</span>
  <span id="freeText10350028117196371982" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.ambsreads.wordpress.com/2018/04/22/aru-shah-and-the-end-of-time-by-roshani-chokshi-review/" rel="nofollow noopener">FIND MY REVIEW FOR ARU SHAH AND THE END OF TIME ON MY BLOG. CLICK HERE TO SEE MORE</a><br /><br />I think I’ve made it pretty clear over time that I am a big fan of Rick Riordan. I love mythology and I love learning through his books. When Riordan announced that he was going to publish own voices authors take on mythology I was beyond excited. Aru Shah and the End of Time was no exception of this. I fell in love, fast. One reason was that it was a female lead, something we don’t typically see in Riordan’s work. An Indian female lead is something that holds incredible importance, and just to see Hindu mythology accurately represented. <br /><br />12-year-old Aru Shah has a habit of telling lies. She lies about basically everything to the people at her school so they don’t look at her as weird, the joys of being middle class in a rich school. One day she’s caught out in the lie when three people from her school come to where she lives – she lives in a museum, like how cool is that?! Things turn pretty nasty quickly with one of these three kids recording Aru as an attempt to get her to tell the truth. Instead, she decides to light a lamp that, as her mother says, is cursed. Unfortunately for Aru, the lamp is cursed. A powerful individual is let free and everyone around her is now frozen in time. With the help of a pigeon guide, Aru discovers she has the soul of the great Pandava brothers. Along the way, Aru meets one of her sisters (because there are no brothers in this generation) and must go on a quest in order to stop the powerful individual she let go free. Simultaneously she must come to terms with being a demigod and how much her mother has hidden from her. Oh, and the best part? Aru must do all this in her spider-man pyjamas as if that isn’t a look.<br /><br />I really loved Aru Shah and the End of Time. It was such a thrilling tale of mystery, surprise and, my favourite, humour. The writing of this particular story came across as pretty flawless. I also know, that if anyone reading this is like me you’re expecting this story to be basically identical to Percy Jackson. I’m here to say you’re wrong. This book completely holds its own and, dare I say it, is even better than Percy Jackson in some ways. It was truly such an important book and I am desperately waiting for book two!<br /><br />Anyway, let me jump into a more detailed version of what I did and didn’t like about Aru Shah and the End of Time by Roshani Chokshi.<br /><br />L I K E S<br />✗ HINDU GODS &gt; GREEK GODS<br /><br />Hear me out, I grew up learning about the Greek gods in school. When I picked up Percy Jackson for the first time I had a big understanding of all the variations. It made it a little boring for me, honestly. I know nothing about Hindu gods. This particular topic wasn’t taught in my schools (I went to 9 over 13 years, as a little fun fact). I know own voices books don’t exist to teach the public anything but I really did love learning about the Hindu gods. I have been deeply curious about the mythology for some time and I don’t trust Google, so it was just great to read something that I was unfamiliar with.<br /><br />Also, the Hindu gods weren’t as big of jerks as the Greek gods in Rick Riordan’s books, also a positive for me.<br /><br />✗ THE CHARACTERS ARE HILARIOUS<br /><br />The humour in this book is amazing. I was giggling and smiling almost the entire book and I’m not even the target audience. It was just such a fun journey that I can’t screech and rave about this book enough. The humour was similar to that of Percy Jackson, dry and most of the time from the main character being unable to shut up, but I just feel as if this particular style was better suited for the target audience. It felt like I could give this book to one of my cousins and she would be laughing along with me.<br /><br />✗ I LOVE BOO<br /><br />Boo is the pigeon guide that Aru and her Pandava sister Mimi are given. He’s not exactly the best guide nor does he really have the patience for two young preteens, but man was he hilarious. His character really brought Mimi and Aru together, and just the whole idea of a pigeon leading two girls on a quest makes me chuckle. To be fair though, I despise birds so the fact I even found this amusing shocks me a little.<br /><br />✗ FEMALE FRIENDSHIPS<br /><br />If you’ve known me for a little while you know I am a big pusher of female friendships in books. I live for them. I love when two girls support one another rather than tearing each other down. Mimi and Aru gave me this. The two are young and it would have been easy to write two girls that hated each other but Roshani Chokshi didn’t, and I loved it. The girls obviously bickered and struggled at some points, but they’d also only just met and been informed they were sisters which can put a strain on any time making friends.<br /><br />2018 is the year of supportive friendships and I’m here for it.<br /><br />✗ CANT WAIT FOR BOOK TWO<br /><br />Do I have to elaborate on this? After the ending of Aru Shah and the End of Time, I desperately have grabby hands for book two. This series will also finish when I’m 24 and if you don’t think I’m going to read every single one, you’re wrong. I am here for this series.<br /><br />D I S L I K E S<br />✗ I FELT ARU SOMETIMES STEPPED BACK IN THE STORY AND HER VOICE GOT LOST<br /><br />I’m really just nitpicking here, but it did feel as if Aru got lost at points. Obviously this a big quest and a whole bit about discovering who you are but I just wanted more. It did seem at points that Aru was morally grey but in truth, she is simply a preteen trying to find her place in the world and her identity. I’m interested to see if she does become morally grey throughout the course of this four book series. I stand by the fact though there should have been a little more focus on Aru’s feelings and emotions at some points.<br /><br />Overall, Aru Shah and the End of Time blew my socks off. I was not expecting anything that this book delivered and I’m slightly annoyed that it took me so long to even pick this up. The hype really stands true for this book, it is well deserving of your money and your time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10350028117196371982" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2387974010" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6203988039180452683">When three classmates show up at her home slash museum of Ancient Indian Art and Culture to confront Aru Shah about lying, she decides to impress them with stories of the artifacts in the museum. Such as the cursed Lamp of Bharata. Trying to save face, she lights the lamp and releases the Sleeper. Now Aru must stop the Sleeper from waking the God of Destruction, or everyone in the world will be frozen in time.<br/><br/><b>The Story-</b><br/>First, let me just say, I loved this book. In the same thread as Rick Riordan</span>
  <span id="freeText6203988039180452683" style="display:none">When three classmates show up at her home slash museum of Ancient Indian Art and Culture to confront Aru Shah about lying, she decides to impress them with stories of the artifacts in the museum. Such as the cursed Lamp of Bharata. Trying to save face, she lights the lamp and releases the Sleeper. Now Aru must stop the Sleeper from waking the God of Destruction, or everyone in the world will be frozen in time.<br><br><b>The Story-</b><br>First, let me just say, I loved this book. In the same thread as Rick Riordan’s Percy Jackson, Chokshi writes the story of a young girl taking on challenges, except this time with Hindu mythology as it’s center. Personally, I think it’s better, but that’s just because I find Greek and Egyptian mythology stuffed down our throats in elementary school. Since I strive to learn more about other countries cultures this was just a treat.<br><br>The story follows Aru Shah as a young girl who just wants to be accepted by her peers and to feel loved by her parent(s). Now if you didn’t feel that way when you were twelve, you’re honestly, probably the oddity here.<br><br>As a middle grade book, this book was just non stop fun. While in the adult mindset I might think- impossible and childish. But in the vein of middle school reads it was just fantastic. From the hilarious chapter titles, the blend of the real world meets Hindu mythology (Such as a the night market being inside of Costco!) to the non stop action as our young heroes (ahem, heroines!) take on challenge after challenge. The book just makes for continuous enjoyment.<br><br><b>The World Building-</b><br>As I said earlier, I adore other cultures, and that includes their mythologies. In the last year I have had the joy of encountering a lot more fantasy that has been inspired by these cultures, and just really adds some extra flavor from the medieval castle with elves type of fantasy.<br><br>If you have never read a Chokshi book, than you probably don’t know, but she does a fantastic job of creating a beautiful creative world that surrounds her characters. The way she writes just add color and life to an ancient world. It’s the type of descriptions that have me daydreaming while I am sitting at work.<br><br>I just loved having these modern day pre-teens running around saving the world and encountering all the things from their bed time stories. There is so much depth to Hindu mythology and I can’t wait to see what Chokshi does in the next book. Regardless, if we had books like this when I was in middle school I think it would have inspired me to kick start my cultural studies at an earlier age.<br><br><b>The Characters-</b><br>Aru Shah is funny. The comments that Aru makes throughout the book had me LOL’ing, because so much of what she says is just the unfiltered thoughts that I would probably have. Except, my mouth is just a little more filtered because you know, adulting can be hard. My favorite thing about Aru was that she was brave. Not in the sense that she can take over the world, but that she was willing to do what it took to save her mom and the rest of the world. She was brave in the face of her failures and confronted them as well.<br><br>Minnie is just a little cupcake. I adore her and her germophobia and brainy ways. I thought she balanced Aru so well by checking her in her wild imaginations while also just being the supporting friend that she needed.<br><br><b>The Soundtrack-</b><br><a href="https://youtu.be/1fn1NOzpwlw" rel="nofollow noopener">SUCRÉ- When We Were Young</a><br><br><a href="https://vicariouslyvoraciously.wordpress.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1506898066i/24064803._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

<div id="review_2360837153" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2360837153" />
    <a title="Kiara Maharaj" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/61766338-kiara-maharaj"><img alt="Kiara Maharaj" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593960483p2/61766338.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2360837153?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kiara Maharaj" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kiara Maharaj" href="/user/show/61766338-kiara-maharaj">Kiara Maharaj</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2360837153" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17347793847891804467">I know this is gonna be one bad review in a million good reviews for this book, but I'm going to share my thoughts on it anyways. Reading this book, I was horrified. I wish I never read it. I put it down several times, but picked it up again because I wanted to see just how far the author will take it. Each page revealed a different atrocity. My last thought when I finished it was "This book needs to be off the shelves, now." <br/><br/>Basically, Valmiki is The Hipster on the Anthill, Hanuman is a big ape</span>
  <span id="freeText17347793847891804467" style="display:none">I know this is gonna be one bad review in a million good reviews for this book, but I'm going to share my thoughts on it anyways. Reading this book, I was horrified. I wish I never read it. I put it down several times, but picked it up again because I wanted to see just how far the author will take it. Each page revealed a different atrocity. My last thought when I finished it was "This book needs to be off the shelves, now." <br /><br />Basically, Valmiki is The Hipster on the Anthill, Hanuman is a big ape who wears a blazer, Urvashi wears a salwar kameez, saat is the number six, the seasons care about instagram, Bollywood is all about slapping each other and "invisible wind", Shakhuni(AKA Shocky) is a freaking pigeon, all the God's vehicles/vahans are stolen, the numbers one and two are dogs in the land of death, pronounced ick and dough, the palace of the Pandav's is an emotional wreck, Dharm Raj's danda is nicknamed Dee Dee, and this is the first of a series of atrocities. <br /><br />First of all, I have a question/s for the author. You claim to be a Hindu. Are you fine with the world dismissing your religion, beliefs, and way of life, as mythology? Are you fine with the western world dumping Hinduism in the same pile they dumped Greek, Roman, Egyptian, and various other mythologies? Are you absolutely fine with the fact that the Hindu Gods are now the content of Rick Riordan's FANDOM WIKI PAGE? Are you fine with the world understanding Hinduism the way you portrayed it in this book - silly, comical, childish, stupid? If a living, breathing, actively practiced religion can be made such a mockery of as you have done to Hinduism in this book, surely the same thing can be done to Christian and Islamic mythology? Or do we dare not call christianity and islam mythology? When last did you watch a Bollywood movie? <br /><br />Why did you write this book?<br /><br />Secondly, I do acknowledge that your research was well conducted, and that the target audience is <br />8-12 year olds. Still, you wouldn't find a christian children's book telling the events of the bible in such a way, where Jesus speaks slang words, shakes his fist, and can't make proper decisions - which, by the way, is how a conversation between Shiv and a demon, Bhasmasura (in the book its spelt Brahmasura) as he asks for a boon, went in the book:<br /><br />Shiva: Why, though?<br />Brahmasura: ☺<br />Shiva: No, seriously, why? That's a horrible wish.<br />Brahmasura: ☺<br />Shiva: I ... ugh. Okay. Fine. You will regret this! *shakes fist*<br />Brahmasura: ☺<br /><br />I was so horrified at this that I actually put the book down to wonder whether I bought a fake, altered copy of the book. No way in history that Shiva was ever portrayed as such. Yet there it was, even though Shiva is such a supreme GOD - as supreme as Jesus to christians. Nobody would write a conversation like that with Jesus, not even in a children's book, now would they? Christians would never tolerate such a thing. So why are we Hindu's tolerating it? Why are we allowing this author to portray our religion like this?<br /><br />That conversation is an excerpt from the glossary section at the end of the book. From the very first page we can witness hordes of things such as the above conversation. The amount of times a "typical Bollywood movie" was described: <br /><br />-page 40: "... she had imagined something from a Bollywood movie. Lights glittering. A wind - out of nowhere - making her hair fly, and everyone breaking into a choreographed song and dance at the exact same time."<br />-page 57: "Vayu, Lord of the Winds, stirred a slight breeze. He was dark skinned and looked like the handsome star of a Bollywood film."<br /> ["Jesus Christ, the Lord and Savior, had a gentle smile on his lips. He was light skinned and looked like the handsome star of a Hollywood film." Note: I assumed his skin complexion based on his race.]<br />-page 134: "3. You could show up like an actor in every Bollywood movie, with an invisible wind blowing through your hair and everyone suddenly dancing around you."<br /> [Something wrong with invisible wind?]<br />-page 200: "Her mother's flight out had been cancelled, and they'd spent the whole day inside, snuggled together on the couch. They'd eaten ramen while watching a Bollywood film where everyone got fake slapped at least once ..."<br />-page 277: "Bollywood: India's version of Hollywood. They produce tons of movies a year. You can always recognize a Bollywood movie, because somebody gets fake-slapped at least once, and every time a musical number starts, the settings changes drastically. (How did they start off dancing in the streets of India and end up in Switzerland by the end of the song?)"<br /> [I suppose the fight scenes in Hollywood movies are real, and they really kill of each other, and musically's like La La Land don't count as people breaking into song and dance at the exact same time.]<br /><br />You wanna watch a good Bollywood movie? I suggest the latest release Padmavaat. Or if you're into action, try Dhoom 3. Comedy? Try Golmaal, or Welcome, or Hera Pheri. Horror? Try Pari. Want to learn about Indian culture from India itself? Try Bajirao Mastani, Chennai Express, Bahubali. Want to learn about Hinduism? Watch the series Mahakali, or Hanuman, or Mahadev. I'm truly curious as to which movies the author watched. <br /><br />But the Bollywood thing is the least of the mockery. Read these descriptions of Hanuman: <br /><br />page 48: "Then there was monkey-faced Hanuman, the trickster who had famously helped the god Rama in his fight against the demon king." <br /> This is true, Hanuman is half monkey and he did help Ram fight the demon Raavan, but do we want the world to refer to Hanuman as "monkey-faced"? And this is describing something called the "Council" (which does not exist in Hinduism) consisting of names like Hanuman, Uloopi, Surasa, Jambavan, Kubera, and Urvashi who are "Guardians" and "worthy of worship but they were often considered seperate from the main league of gods and goddesses" - please tell me when Hanuman was ever considered separate. The GOD who we chant and dedicate the Hanuman Chalisa to? And according to this book, the council "gather on Tuesdays and Thursdays, and during full moons and new moons, and also for the season premiere and finale of Game of Thrones." Would anyone ever dare to say that Jesus and his apostles gather to watch Game of Thrones???<br /><br />page 279: "Hanuman (HUH-noo-mahn) One of the main figures in the Indian epic the Ramayana, who was known for his devotion to the god-king Rama and Rama's wife, Sita. Hanuman is the son of Vayu, the god of the wind, and Anjana, an apsara. He had lots of mischievious exploits as a kid, including mistaking the sun for a mango and trying to eat it. There are still temples shrines dedicated to Hanuman and he's often worshipped by wrestlers because of his incredible strength. He's the half brother of Bhima, the second-oldest Pandava brother."<br /> [Once again, I acknowledge the author's research.]<br /><br />page 281: "...it describes how the god-king Rama, aided by his brother and the monkey-faced demigod Hanuman ..."<br />page 282: "Vayu is also the father of Hanuman, the monkeyfaced demigod."<br />page 269: " "This way," said the monkey-faced demigod, bounding ahead of them."<br /><br />But perhaps the most peeving part of Hanuman's description was his entrance(he and urvashi enter at the same time, and they are having a conversation):<br />page 50:<br />" To the left of the celestial dancer, a deep voice let out a powerful laugh."You really hold on to a grudge, don't you? Hasn't it been a millenium since he ruined your outfit?" The monkey demigod Hanuman materialized in his throne. He was wearing a silk blazer and a shirt patterned with forest leaves. His tail flopped over the back of his chair, and from one of his ears dangled a jewel that looked like a small crown.<br />"It wasn't my outfit, you big ape," snapped Urvashi. <br /> [Silk blazer??? Shirt patterned with forest leaves???? You big ape?????!!! Hanuman looked up to Urvashi as a mother. Author, again I ask you, do you want the world to see Hanuman wearing a freaking silk blazer? This is how he looks:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.thedivineindia.com/img/shri-hanuman-ji.jpg">https://www.thedivineindia.com/img/sh...</a><br /><br />As for Urvashi: <br /> <br />page 50: "Aru turned to see the most beautiful woman in the world sitting on the throne labeled URVASHI. She wore black leggings and a salwar kameez top that would have appeared as simple as white spun cotton if it didn't glimmer like woven moonlight. Around her ankles was a set of gunghroo bells. She was tall and dark-skinned and wore her hair in a messy braid. She looked as if she'd just stepped out of dance rehearsal. Which, given the fact that she was the chief dancer of the heavens, was probably true."<br /> Salwar Kameez? Seriously? Not to mention that she gives Aru and Mini and MEHENDHI MAP. Why are you working on such stereotypical ideas of Indians? <br />This is an actor who played Urvashi in the series Sankatmochan Mahabali Hanuman (Note: NO SALWAR KAMEEZ): <br /> <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://i.ytimg.com/vi/40tlfnvvTlM/hqdefault.jpg">https://i.ytimg.com/vi/40tlfnvvTlM/hq...</a><br /><br />Among more childish and stupidly portrayed scenes: <br />-Draupadi coming home to her five husbands, page 60: "Imagine walking in your front door, calling out, Honey, are you home? and hearing: Yes dear! Yes dear! Yes dear! Yes dear! Yes dear!<br />-Arjun invading his wife and brother's privacy when it was their year to spend together, page 61: "He could've just knocked on the door and shouted, Bro, I left my bow and arrow. Could you hand 'em to me? It'd be like asking a friend to pass you some toilet paper under the stall if you're in a pinch."<br />-Hanuman describing his childhood, page 66: "When I was young I mistook the sun for a fruit. Got in a lot of trouble for that," he said, sounding more pleased with himself than guilt-ridden. "I clashed with a planet, and threw off a scheduled eclipse. Your father, Indra, was so mad that he used his famous lightning bolt to strike me down from the sky. It hit me in the side of the face, which is how I earned the name Hanuman, or 'Prominent jaw'."<br />-Describing the first time Shiv and Ganesh met: "A Parvati is getting their home ready for Shiva's return, she tells Ganesh not to let anyone through the door(Guests can be a nuisance.) So Ganesh, being a good kid, says "Okay!" When Shiva strides up to the door, shouting, "Honeyyyy, I'm hooooome!" Ganesh and Shiva look at each other, frown, and at the same time say "And you do you think you are?" .... "Shiva lops of Ganesh's head. Which I can only imagine was supremely awakward for the family. To avoid a big fight with Parvati, Shiva goes out and grabs an elephant's head, sticks it on his son's body, and bam, now its fine. <br /><br />If that does not sound like mockery. Seriously. It's actual sentences in the book. Dear Author, you are making Hinduism sound like rubbish stories that have no moral intent, no teachings, no essence. Why did you write this book?<br /><br />I don't understand what other readers find interesting or thrilling about this book, or the story. If the world thinks that Hinduism as portrayed in this book is interesting, what would they say when they really start reading about Hinduism? If Harry Potter was burned because it portrayed witchcraft and sorcery, this book should too. I want this book to be banned and the series stopped. Plain and simple. <br /><br />Hinduism is not "underrepresented" - maybe in the west it is, but I'm definitely NOT supporting this book, Aru Shah and the End of Time, to stand as a representation. Hinduism is not "mythology" - its not dead, the way the west killed the greek gods. if Rick Riordan dismisses the living religion as such, then the same should be done to christianity and islam. Hindus are being quiet. But - bring on the Rick Riordan imprint of christian and islamic mythology, and then watch the uproar.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17347793847891804467" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1983327647" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1983327647" />
    <a title="Taylor" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52489703-taylor"><img alt="Taylor" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1542815566p2/52489703.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1983327647?book_show_action=true">Apr 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Taylor" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Taylor" href="/user/show/52489703-taylor">Taylor</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52489703-taylor?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52489703-taylor?shelf=2018-books">2018-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52489703-taylor?shelf=mythology-books">mythology-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1983327647" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9658393475779021435"><i>"Suddenly, the world she thought she knew had opened up, as if stage curtains had been yanked back to show her that there was so much <b>more</b> than what she'd imagined. There was magic. Secrets crouched in the dark. Characters from stories, like the ones she'd been told all her life, were taking off their masks and saying, <b>I was never a tale, but the truth.</b></i>"<br/><br/>...<br/><br/><i>Aru Shah and the End of Time</i> was one of my most anticipated releases of 2018, and it didn't disappoint. Let me just get this out of the way: </span>
  <span id="freeText9658393475779021435" style="display:none"><i>"Suddenly, the world she thought she knew had opened up, as if stage curtains had been yanked back to show her that there was so much <b>more</b> than what she'd imagined. There was magic. Secrets crouched in the dark. Characters from stories, like the ones she'd been told all her life, were taking off their masks and saying, <b>I was never a tale, but the truth.</b></i>"<br /><br />...<br /><br /><i>Aru Shah and the End of Time</i> was one of my most anticipated releases of 2018, and it didn't disappoint. Let me just get this out of the way: <b>if you love Rick Riordan's books, read this.</b> It's a colorful, lovely story steeped with rich Hindu mythology, and <b>I couldn't get enough of it.</b><br /><br />In this first book, we follow a young seventh grader named Aru, and she's a <i>bit</i> of a liar. She lives in the Museum of Ancient Indian Art and Culture in Atlanta, and her mother is the museum's curator. Unlike her wealthy classmates, Aru will be spending her Autumn break at home. <br /><br />And like I said: Aru has a habit of fudging the truth to make her <i>own</i> reality more colorful and interesting. This backfires when four of her classmates come to the museum to catch her in a lie, and they end up daring her to light the ancient Lamp of Bharata. Even though her mother has warned her not to, Aru lights the lamp, freezing time and freeing the Sleeper, who is intent on awakening the God of Destruction.<br /><br />So yeah, <b>Aru's Autumn break has gotten off to a bad start.</b><br /><br />I will admit, the first 100 pages of this book were fun, but I wasn't <i>completely</i> immersed. It wasn't until about a third of the way through that Aru's story wholly sucked me in; there's a scene in <i>Aru Shah</i> that really...surprised me, and it gave a depth to the story that I wasn't expecting. <b>From that point on, I absolutely loved this book.</b><br /><br />It is no surprise that Roshani's writing in here was beautiful, <b>but oh man, was it lovely.</b> I excessively tabbed my copy of this book, and I <i>rarely</i> ever do that. And for a middle grade? Not likely.<br /><br />The flowery, humorous prose, paired with the rich Hindu mythology entangled throughout this story, made <i>Aru Shah and the End of Time</i> a truly wonderful reading experience. This is the most well-written middle grade book I've ever read, and <b>I will continue to read anything Roshani writes.</b><br /><br />As far as comparisons go, <i>Percy Jackson</i> meets Sailor Moon is <b>completely spot on</b>, especially if you consider what's to come in later books. A badass girl-gang of Indian demigods destined to save the world? <b>YES PLEASE.</b> <br /><br />And like Rick Riordan's mythology-centered YA and middle grade stories, this book was <b>incredibly funny</b>. That's due in part to Aru's humorous and ironically honest inner monolgue. Also, I'm going mention Boo the talking Pigeon for a second: not only was he <b>hilarious and comically self-righteous</b>, but he also developed a very sweet connection with two of our main characters.<br /><br />Yep, Aru has another young girl that she teams up with on this adventure. Unlike Aru Shah, who is loud, opinionated, and imaginative, Mini is...<b>not</b>. She's allergic to everything, has a big fear of death (don't we all), and is maybe too smart for her own good. <b>But oh, did I love her for it.</b> Both girls are wonderful in their own way, and I adored their friendship. <b>There's no romance in this book: just a lovely friendship between two girls.</b> Thank the gods.<br /><br />The action was exciting. The plot was full of adventure and whimsy and strange, dreamlike imagery. The Hindu mythology was <b>fascinating</b>, and I can't wait to get more from this world, from these wonderful characters. <br /><br />I have no doubt that the Pandava Quartet will be an amazing middle grade fantasy series. And now, I will anxiously wait for <i>Aru Shah and the Song of Death.</i> <b>I can't wait.</b><br /><br />...<br /><br /><i>Boo fluttered to Mini's shoulder. "Well, that's not how the legendary Arjuna would've done it." <br /><br />"I'm not Arjuna," said Aru, lifting her chin. "I'm Aru."<br /><br />Boo puffed out his chest. "I know."</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="9658393475779021435" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
